  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5ee3dc90-5f39-4ea6-8969-db73333fff7f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <span id="freeText7100678667705630716" style="display:none">Macey McHenry—Glamorous society girl or spy-in-training?<br /><br />W.W. Hale V—Heir to an American dynasty or master thief?<br /><br />There are two sides to every coin. Whether these two can work together is a tossup.<br /><br />Born into privilege, Macey and Hale are experts at mingling with the upper class. But even if they’ve never raised an eyebrow at the glitz, neither teenager has ever felt at home with the glamour.<br /><br />When Macey and Hale meet at a society gala, the party takes a dangerous turn. Suddenly they’re at the center of a hostage situation, and it’s up to them to stop the thugs from becoming hostile. Will Macey’s spy skills and Hale’s con-man ways be enough to outsmart a ruthless gang? Or will they have to seek out the ultimate inside girl to help?<br /><br />The worlds of Heist Society and the Gallagher Girls collide in Ally Carter’s fast-paced, high-stakes and tantalizing new story. Get a behind the scenes glimpse as Ally delivers an irresistible thriller that is full of her signature style and savvy twists.</span>

    <a title="mara • (chaotic reader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12902362-mara-chaotic-reader"><img alt="mara • (chaotic reader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493058074p2/12902362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/474876230?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mara • (chaotic reader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mara • (chaotic reader)" href="/user/show/12902362-mara-chaotic-reader">mara • (chaotic reader)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People new to Ally's books, old Ally fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12902362-mara-chaotic-reader?shelf=assassins-and-spies">assassins-and-spies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer474876230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2911614559587979769"><b>For those looking for a link to Ally's free novella:</b><br/><a href='http://spiesandthieves.com/pdf/Double_Crossed.pdf' rel='nofollow noopener'>click here to get yourself some Hale</a><br/>(Note: the novella was released completely free for everyone by the publishers. So thank you Ally!)<br/><br/>What a perfect little novella! The combination of Hale and Macey is brilliant - I NEED THEM TO APPEAR TOGETHER AGAIN. Not as a couple or anything like that, just as a badass duo. I mean imagine this: both have a don't-give-a-damn attitude, both are witty and both have that badass sexy edge. Perfect team.<br/><br/><b>So here </b></span>
  <span id="freeText2911614559587979769" style="display:none"><b>For those looking for a link to Ally's free novella:</b><br><a href="http://spiesandthieves.com/pdf/Double_Crossed.pdf" rel="nofollow noopener">click here to get yourself some Hale</a><br>(Note: the novella was released completely free for everyone by the publishers. So thank you Ally!)<br><br>What a perfect little novella! The combination of Hale and Macey is brilliant - I NEED THEM TO APPEAR TOGETHER AGAIN. Not as a couple or anything like that, just as a badass duo. I mean imagine this: both have a don't-give-a-damn attitude, both are witty and both have that badass sexy edge. Perfect team.<br><br><b>So here you have our beloved Hale:</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>He was tall, with broad shoulders and careless hair, in a designer tuxedo that he wore as if it was simply what he'd found on the floor by his bed that morning. With his roguish smile and cool indifference . . .</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>And then we have Macey:</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>Macey McHenry was sidling up to him. She looked like a bored society girl who was in the mood to grab the nearest guy and leave the party. But if there was anything W.W. Hale V truly understood, it was that looks could often be deceiving.<br>As soon as she was close she whispered, "You've got to get out of here."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I also loved how the reader got a glimpse of how Kat and Hale's relationship has developed since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10327303.Uncommon_Criminals__Heist_Society___2_" title="Uncommon Criminals (Heist Society, #2) by Ally Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Uncommon Criminals</a>.<br><b>Just look at them:</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Who is that?" Macey asked.<br>"The reason I wasn't flirting with you," Hale told her.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><br>__________________________________<br><br><i><b>PRE-READING 10/12/2012:</b><br>A CROSSOVER? DID SOMEONE SAY CROSSOVER? YES? YES! Ally Carter's books are always so entertaining and fun to read. <br><br>But spies and thieves in the same book <s>or rather novella</s>? Are you sure this is safe Ally? <i>Are you really really sure?</i> This much sexiness and danger can't be healthy? Am I right ladies?<br><br>I mean <b>Hale </b> you sauve little 16 year old. Why can't all 16 year old boys be like you? I can't describe the extent of my literary crush on him.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392665ra/755927.gif" width="250" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2911614559587979769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_655308908" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/655308908" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/655308908?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=nook">nook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer655308908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15825618776125893035"><br/><i>Thanks to NetGalley for a copy of this book</i><br/><br/>For those of you who don't know, Ally Carter is the young adult author of The Gallagher Girls (a series about an academy that trains teenage girls to be spies) and The Heist Society ( an Ocean's Elevenish series about teenage thieves). Double Crossed is the highly anticipated crossover novella that brings these two different groups together.<br/><i>*insert squealing tween fangirls here*</i><br/>I've never read any of the Gallagher Girls books, but I <i>have</i> read the first </span>
  <span id="freeText15825618776125893035" style="display:none"><br><i>Thanks to NetGalley for a copy of this book</i><br><br>For those of you who don't know, Ally Carter is the young adult author of The Gallagher Girls (a series about an academy that trains teenage girls to be spies) and The Heist Society ( an Ocean's Elevenish series about teenage thieves). Double Crossed is the highly anticipated crossover novella that brings these two different groups together.<br><i>*insert squealing tween fangirls here*</i><br>I've never read any of the Gallagher Girls books, but I <i>have</i> read the first book in the Heist Society. While I thought it was cute, it didn't really inspire me to run out and grab any more of Carter's stuff. However, after reading this, I might just change my mind.<br><br>Alrighty, you have two society kids at a charity function, and both are more than they seem at first glance. When a group of gunmen take the room hostage, they each utilize their own different set of skills to bring the bad guys down.<br><i>*insert theme from Mission Impossible here*</i><br><br>The story itself was surprisingly fun. And I say <i>surprising</i>, because I am nowhere near the age of the intended target audience. No, it's not gonna blow your mind, but it was really good for a novella. And since it's short, it's a good way to see if these might be something you'd be interested in, without having to commit to a full-size book. I don't think prior knowledge of the characters is a must, either. I recognized Hale from the Heist Society, but I had no idea who Macey was, since she's a Gallagher Girl. It didn't impact my enjoyment of the story at all, but there may have been a few inside jokes that I missed.<br>I'd recommend this for anyone looking for a fast-paced easy read, or maybe just looking for a book for that special tweenage girl in your life.<br><br><div>
  <a href="http://www.addicted2heroines.com/2013/07/double-crossed-spies-and-thieves-story.html" title="Addicted 2 Heroines" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412937777i/11444542.jpg" alt="Addicted 2 Heroines" width="100%" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_493037283" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/493037283" />
    <a title="Jasprit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit"><img alt="Jasprit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456315622p2/4841793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/493037283?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasprit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasprit" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit">Jasprit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=out-2013">out-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer493037283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17386818905410757117">Not being a huge fan of the Gallagher Girls series and a huge fan of the Heist society series. I was a little worried that maybe this book wouldn’t be for me, but I was wrong as Carter produces a brilliant mash up of two different worlds in Double Crossed. <br/><br/>Macey and Hale find themselves in the wrong place at the wrong time, what was meant to be a friendly auction turns into all the guests being held hostage by a bunch of robbers who will stop at nothing to get what they want. Despite our favouri</span>
  <span id="freeText17386818905410757117" style="display:none">Not being a huge fan of the Gallagher Girls series and a huge fan of the Heist society series. I was a little worried that maybe this book wouldn’t be for me, but I was wrong as Carter produces a brilliant mash up of two different worlds in Double Crossed. <br /><br />Macey and Hale find themselves in the wrong place at the wrong time, what was meant to be a friendly auction turns into all the guests being held hostage by a bunch of robbers who will stop at nothing to get what they want. Despite our favourite characters finding themselves in a tight situation, Carter was able to sprinkle the story with humour which resulted in a light hearted, fun and enjoyable read. It was great seeing sets of characters having to be forced to work together in a situation when they didn’t trust one other the least bit. Both Macey and Hale didn’t know what the other had up their sleeve but were able to put their brilliant minds together and find a way to get out of the dire situation. What I enjoyed the most about Double Crossed aside the brilliant pacing and cons was the relationship between Hale and Kat. It was great to have both of them finally to be open about their feelings for one another. <br /><br />Double Crossed was a quick story which will be sure to delight fans of Ally Carter’s previous series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17386818905410757117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1316580-ana"><img alt="Ana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491291179p2/1316580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/496697454?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana" href="/user/show/1316580-ana">Ana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1316580-ana?shelf=zz-netgalley">zz-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1316580-ana?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer496697454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12928769817769595526"><b>5 stars</b><br/><br/>Ever since Ms. Carter first mentioned this book I was really looking forward to reading it. A clash of Gallagher Girls and Heist Society? What's not to like there? :D So, I was overjoyed when I noticed it on NetGalley (and no requesting needed) :-) .<br/><br/>OK, on to the story itself. Imagine an ordinary society gala. A lot of rich, influential people wandering around. Filled to brims with women adorned in millions of dollars worth of diamonds. And one woman, the proud owner of the Canary diamond</span>
  <span id="freeText12928769817769595526" style="display:none"><b>5 stars</b><br><br>Ever since Ms. Carter first mentioned this book I was really looking forward to reading it. A clash of Gallagher Girls and Heist Society? What's not to like there? :D So, I was overjoyed when I noticed it on NetGalley (and no requesting needed) :-) .<br><br>OK, on to the story itself. Imagine an ordinary society gala. A lot of rich, influential people wandering around. Filled to brims with women adorned in millions of dollars worth of diamonds. And one woman, the proud owner of the Canary diamond shines brighter than of all them.<br><blockquote>
  <span>[image error]</span>
</blockquote><br>Sounds like a thief's dream, doesn't it? Well, some would definitely agree, since they actually did decide to relive the guest of their valuables. What they didn't do is count on Macey McHenry and W.W. Hale V.<br><br>Macey is bored to tears. Her friends aren't with her, and there's nobody interesting or new in the place. Unless, wait - who is that gorgeous guy and is he stealing something from a guest?<br><br>Hale isn't thrilled with the gala either. There's no challenge in her - except for the strange girl who is more than she appears. There is something odd about her, but figuring out what it is would have to wait since the guys with guns showed up. <br><blockquote>
  <span>[image error]</span>
</blockquote><br>I adore this story! Seeing the two worlds clash is even better than I imagined. <br><br>I liked how well all of them worked together. They didn't trust each other immediately (after all they are all pretty paranoid because of their jobs), but at the end they managed to pull off a perfect plan (one worthy of Kat). <br><br>Hale is as dreamy and gorgeous as ever - not long now for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13580928.Perfect_Scoundrels__Heist_Society___3_" title="Perfect Scoundrels (Heist Society, #3) by Ally Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Perfect Scoundrels</a>. And Macey, well she made waiting for the next book in the Gallagher Girls series even more of a torture.<br><br>All in all, an amazing short story that will make you crave more of Ms. Carter's writing!<br><br><i>ARC received from Disney Book Group via NetGalley.</i><br></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_521762840" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/521762840" />
    <a title="Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6665735-books"><img alt="Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419956881p2/6665735.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/521762840?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Books" href="/user/show/6665735-books">Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6665735-books?shelf=reviewed-2013">reviewed-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6665735-books?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer521762840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10314174408573468507">Anyone who has read the Heist Society series or Gallagher Girls series by author Ally Carter will more than likely agree that this novella, which collaborates characters from both these series, are a genius idea. I, on the other hand, haven’t yet read either of these series’ but after reading three chapters from each of the first books as bonus material in Double Crossed, I am eagerly looking forward to getting started on both. <br/><br/>That said, I enjoyed the sneak peeks of Heist Society and Gallagher </span>
  <span id="freeText10314174408573468507" style="display:none">Anyone who has read the Heist Society series or Gallagher Girls series by author Ally Carter will more than likely agree that this novella, which collaborates characters from both these series, are a genius idea. I, on the other hand, haven’t yet read either of these series’ but after reading three chapters from each of the first books as bonus material in Double Crossed, I am eagerly looking forward to getting started on both. <br /><br />That said, I enjoyed the sneak peeks of Heist Society and Gallagher Girls and as this is the first time I’ve read anything by Ally Carter, I can see why her books receive so much hype. In Double Crossed her impeccable writing style had me hooked from the word go, and her characters are lifelike and authentic. The author strays from overused clichés when it comes to character descriptions, and gives readers freedom to use their imagination in immersing themselves in a high society setting as it suits them. Using details sparingly, but highlighting the important ones to ground the reader, she takes us into a world which feels convincingly real and makes you feel right at home as though you’ve always been a part of it. The witty banter between Macey and Hale is heart-warming and I’m so darn grateful the author didn’t set them up as love-at-first-sight or characters who are instantly attracted to each other. Each character gets a turn to shine and combining their individual “talents”, they make a kick-ass team. In the space of eight chapters I’ve gotten to know Hale, Macey and Kat so well, it feels as though I’ve known them forever.<br /><br />A clever plot, three unforgettable characters, and a lot of imaginative twists, have me uber excited to find out what Heist Society and Gallagher Girls are all about! This is one read I’ll definitely be highly recommending to friends and fellow bookworms alike. <br /><br />I received a free copy of this novella from the publisher, via Netgalley, in exchange for an honest review.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10314174408573468507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4987597416511763769">Gallagher Girls meet Heist Society! Wow! This was such a fun short-story! If you like the Gallagher Girls series(which I love!) and you like The Heist Society(which I also love!) then you must read this book from Ally Carter.<br/><br/> Hale(from Heist Society) and Macey(from the Gallagher Girls Academy) are both at the Calloway Ball when a group of gunmen dressed in Presidential masks take the group hostage.   <span id="freeText4987597416511763769" style="display:none">Gallagher Girls meet Heist Society! Wow! This was such a fun short-story! If you like the Gallagher Girls series(which I love!) and you like The Heist Society(which I also love!) then you must read this book from Ally Carter.<br /><br /> Hale(from Heist Society) and Macey(from the Gallagher Girls Academy) are both at the Calloway Ball when a group of gunmen dressed in Presidential masks take the group hostage. The scheme seems much more elaborate than just a normal grab the jewels and run type job. Hale and Macey join forces to thwart the thieves. Of course they have a little outside help from Kat and Abby. The thieves don't have a chance once the spy girl and the con join forces!<br /><br />What a fun idea to link the two series together! I enjoyed it very much and am looking forward to the next installment of The Heist Society "Perfect Scoundrels" coming out February 5th. I haven't heard when the next Gallagher Girls book will be coming out, but definitely will be watching for it.<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer514434552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8589052739713536476">What an ambitious thing to do - incorporate your two very different series into one novella. I really liked the Heist Society books and was excited to hear there's going to be another one coming out soon. And I've never read the Gallagher Girls, but after reading this novella, I am definitely curious.<br/><br/>I really like Carter's intricate planning - each little step that she is careful to set up to where it works out so well in the whole story. And I wasn't crazy about it at first, but her "no one not</span>
  <span id="freeText8589052739713536476" style="display:none">What an ambitious thing to do - incorporate your two very different series into one novella. I really liked the Heist Society books and was excited to hear there's going to be another one coming out soon. And I've never read the Gallagher Girls, but after reading this novella, I am definitely curious.<br /><br />I really like Carter's intricate planning - each little step that she is careful to set up to where it works out so well in the whole story. And I wasn't crazy about it at first, but her "no one notices when" is a really good way of pointing out things because it's hard to visualize what's happening if you're not paying attention to what you need to.<br /><br />I'm not usually a fan of novellas, but I'm just impressed because you wouldn't think a 90-page book would make your gears churning.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8589052739713536476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_474802248" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/474802248" />
    <a title="Caroline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7245479-caroline"><img alt="Caroline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370010792p2/7245479.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/474802248?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline" href="/user/show/7245479-caroline">Caroline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7245479-caroline?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7245479-caroline?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7245479-caroline?shelf=young-adult-contemporary">young-adult-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7245479-caroline?shelf=spies-and-assassins">spies-and-assassins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7245479-caroline?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer474802248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11913427433084766330">omg<br/><br/>Should I count how many times I almost ended up on the floor from the amount of cute?<br/><br/>"""""""The reason I wasn't flirting with you."""""""""<br/><br/>Look, that's my review. That's it.<br/><br/>Not going to lie, my favourite Goodreads shelf is broody-rich-boys-aka-w-w-hale-v<br/><br/>Do I quote this entire novella????? Because it was great.<br/><br/>omg<br/><br/>Everyone's really hot.<br/><br/>""""""What's your name?"""""" <br/>"You'd be surprised how many times I get asked that question." <br/><br/>jfc *___*<br/><br/>You two, stop it. <br/><br/>This is what the world would look like if</span>
  <span id="freeText11913427433084766330" style="display:none">omg<br /><br />Should I count how many times I almost ended up on the floor from the amount of cute?<br /><br />"""""""The reason I wasn't flirting with you."""""""""<br /><br />Look, that's my review. That's it.<br /><br />Not going to lie, my favourite Goodreads shelf is broody-rich-boys-aka-w-w-hale-v<br /><br />Do I quote this entire novella????? Because it was great.<br /><br />omg<br /><br />Everyone's really hot.<br /><br />""""""What's your name?"""""" <br />"You'd be surprised how many times I get asked that question." <br /><br />jfc *___*<br /><br />You two, stop it. <br /><br />This is what the world would look like if Kat Bishop didn't exist. It’s okay, AU is okay but Kat :') :') :’) :’) I love you. (And Hale.) (Macey too.) <br /><br />Also!!!!!!!!!! Abby.<br /><br />Ladies everywhere.<br /><br /><b>"It's a sisterhood."</b><br /><br />This (”It’s a sisterhood”) is basically what Gallagher Girls is about. Because it's a sisterhood and it transcends generations, and you get girls and ladies everywhere who are so great that I don't know how to handle them. I don't know. <br /><br />Because it's about a school that teaches girls to become spies, and they learn to fight for all the things they think they should fight for. And they don't let anyone else tell them otherwise. Because even though there are also great adult characters in both series, but especially GG, these adults don't shape these girls nor are they resented or missing from their lives or the cause of their angst. These girls look up to them, and sometimes worship them, but they make their own choices in the end, even when the whole world is telling them teenagers can't be the heroes, that teenage girls cannot be the ones who win, especially against adults who kill and just don't care. So some of these girls do things that hurt their parents because they believe in what they're doing, and the adults love them still (but they also hurt because these girls are their daughters and how can you not???).<br /><br />THESE GIRLS UGH. These girls love each other, and every one of them is flawed but they're also so, so, so great (which is the only way tbh). And every one of them has their own character arc, even the adults, and it's beautiful. Even the minor characters all get their time to shine, but these girls are the ones who are the true heroes. And some of them come from heartbreaking backgrounds, some who are running from their family, and some who are running towards, and sometimes they get lost, or think they know what they’re doing, but it doesn’t matter. Because it’s them, and they’re all that matters. These girls are their own people, but they become – not complete because a person is never a half of themselves without another person – but just <i>more</i>.<br /><br />Also the emphasis on POSITIVE female friendships in general. Because sometimes there is so much hate between girls in YA, like, "Wow you like the boy I like, you are obviously not a deserving person," or "the mean girl vs the main character girl" or slut-shaming (which is actually the worst because the state of a girl's virginity should not be the measure of her character), but these girls, these four - oh my God. <br /><br />Just - Cammie, Bex, Liz and Macey, and how much they love each other. <br /><br />How different and ""strong"" they are because they make each other strong – don’t even go there with “strong female characters” because you lose me there. They are strong, not because they are physically strong and definitely not because they aren’t emotional (because there are far too many times where I see girls derided as “weak” and “annoying” and “over-emotional” for even daring to feel (How dare they??) – but because they make each other strong. How they work with each other, and pick each other up, but also admire, get angry at each other, but most of all, that they all know that they can be so much more when the four of them are together.<br /><br />There's sister feelings as well with Aunt Abby and Rachel. Because it is a sisterhood that links generations and generations of Gallagher Girls. And these two sisters are such an epitome of that, that they’re best friends, best partners, and love each other so, so much.<br /><br />Omg, also mothers!! Mothers and their daughters, girls and their mothers etc and these books, especially Cammie's character and arc, and basically her entire relationship with her mother. JUST. Every single Gallagher Girl ever. <br /><br />And....and.......and, the relationships in both Heist Society and Gallagher Girls between Kat/Hale and Cammie/Zach. Because there isn't a dominant person of the relationship who the supposedly "weaker" one is meant to rely on; there isn't an imbalance between one who might be physically, mentally superior with desired skills, to the one that is so-called "normal." Because even this trope, is turned on its head with Kat and Hale’s relationship because Hale is the one who chooses Kat and has to learn her family’s trade, while Kat was born into it and is experienced in the only way that is passed down in the family. And how Hale sort of reveres Kat for all the things she can do, and just their belief in each other, and how they're a team but how they also both balance each other and how Hale and Kat can be forces individually but when they’re together, it’s as if the world rights itself. (And this is the way it should be. A person should not be “your other half” because it suggests that you were never whole until you met them, but someone who, once they’ve walked into your life, you can’t ever imagine your life without them in it ever again.)<br /><br />And with Zach/Cammie, and how Cammie recognises that Zach knows all these things she doesn't, she knows that in their trade, that in espionage, some things are better kept hidden, and that some things you don't want to overhear but have to be told. But!!!!!! How this doesn't stop her from getting frustrated, punching and fighting when she needs to; it doesn't lend her a disadvantage because she knows things and she is smart and awesome in all the ways that Zach can't be. And because it is reinforced over and over again that she also has her mum and Bex and Macey and Liz and her sisterhood, and she would not trade them to know all the secrets in the world.<br /><br />Ok.<br /><br />Continuing with Zach and Cammie I guess, and how their relationship is portrayed where women are their equals, if not better than their male counterparts (!!!!!!!! Gallagher Academy is a school that was founded on one lady's protest that girls could be better fighters, better spies than men – like, what more do you want?????). Where women are the strong ones but how they're also weak. Where men are the strong ones but how they're also weak. Because it is wrong to say that just because you are a boy or girl or anywhere on the gender spectrum, that doesn't define what you are supposed to ~~feel~ or be. And like, Zach? Keep treating your girlfriend (??? girlfriend?? I don't know, it's complicated) like an equal. It's really hot.<br /><br />And Zach, but probably more Hale to an extent, especially in Double Crossed, both know that they're dating queens of the world. (And they also wouldn’t have it any other way.)<br /><br />And there isn't an instance in any of these series where the girl has to love the guy "for her own good". Or has to love him because he told her so, because there are so many ways that it could’ve gone down this path because omg, “we’re the only two who can keep each other safe,” or something like this. And you know what? This series isn't even about romantic relationships. But about a sisterhood. And how that's all you need. And sometimes you are better off with just your friends and family, because you might become a better person because of it. That it might be healthier to be alone or with no one. <br /><br />However, that is not to say that the guys aren't great because they are. ALLY CARTER CREATES REALLY REALLY GR8 MALE LOVE INTERESTS. YOU JUST HAVE NO IDEA WHAT YOU ARE MISSING.<br /><br />Especially in Double Crossed (lol, I think I was actually supposed to be talking about this in the first place), where Hale and Macey are so ugh, I don't even know. They're so, you can't compare them???? Because they are both different and better at different things. And they argue and no one really comes out the wiser. I don't know how to explainnnnnnn. There's banter and suspicion, weaponising beauty and sexuality on both sides which is my fave. But also a lot of battling of the wits and who is better at all this covert operations stuff, and it's just so funny and excellent it makes me want to cry.<br /><br />But, I just want everyone to read these books. <br /><br />Just - don't let the first book of the Gallagher Girls series put you off the rest!!! I pity those who do not read Gallager Girls after "I'd Tell You I'd Love You, but then I'd have to Kill You." It's the weakest link in the chain and probably the weakest plot-wise imo, but also one that can't be not read. As I said before, these characters get so much love because all these books develop them and because they all grow and learn and things change and they have to deal with it. And sometimes it's incredibly sad but they manage. Because girls, especially teenage girls, are not the weak ones.<br /><br />Sigh.<br /><br />Just.<br /><br />Women everywhere.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11913427433084766330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_514520997" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/514520997" />
    <a title="Em" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14115059-em"><img alt="Em" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351669486p2/14115059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/514520997?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Em" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Em" href="/user/show/14115059-em">Em</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14115059-em?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14115059-em?shelf=awesome-books">awesome-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer514520997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6298254286170080464">Okay, so I haven't read an Ally Carter book since early last year when GG5 first came out. But reading this novella simply reminded me exactly why I fell in love with Ally Carter's writing. Simply put, she's amazing! Her storylines are intriguing and mysterious and the characters are funny and captivating and makes you wish you knew people like them or are them. ;) And everytime one of my questions such as <i>'Oh no why is Hale pushing his mother into an elevator?!'</i> has been answered another one po</span>
  <span id="freeText6298254286170080464" style="display:none">Okay, so I haven't read an Ally Carter book since early last year when GG5 first came out. But reading this novella simply reminded me exactly why I fell in love with Ally Carter's writing. Simply put, she's amazing! Her storylines are intriguing and mysterious and the characters are funny and captivating and makes you wish you knew people like them or are them. ;) And everytime one of my questions such as <i>'Oh no why is Hale pushing his mother into an elevator?!'</i> has been answered another one pops up <i>(the last elevator slid slowly open and two men in masks rushed out.)</i> to keep me interested till the very last page and goes to show why she's an awesome author!<br /><br />In Double Crossed, we get to read some parts in Hale's POV, which is just so cool, I can't even begin to tell you how much! We also see exactly how he feels towards Kat. Which is a lot more obvious through the use of Macey's POV ;)But don't get me wrong his still the same charming, flirtatous, swoonworthy W. W. Hale V that we love! And his still delivering those wonderful comments we just love, such as this one... <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[“You’re late,” Kat said as soon as Hale put the phone to his ear. She wasn’t the kind of girl to wait for hello. <br />“What can I say? Macey McHenry has been throwing herself at me….” <br />“See, that’s the kind of thing that would make me jealous if she weren’t way out of your league.”<br />“You know, if I had feelings, that might have hurt them.” <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />As much as I would have loved to see Zach and Cammie in this novella. I still think it's so awesome that Macey and Abby are in it to add that Gallagher girl touch to the book as well as their character personalities that we love, such as Macey's covert skills and why she's kickass and Abby's awesome intuition such as finding who the bad guy is, which I would have never guessed! Because I'm pretty sure throughout the whole novella, my brain was trying to pick a side of either spies or thief's...And I still can't choose! <br /><br />But the ending...oh man the ending! Ally Carter, I have just got to say, that is such an AWESOME ending! It was sweet, mysterious and alluring! I mean how totally awesome would it be if Katarina Bishop was a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Gallagher girl <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>?!<br /><br />After reading this novella I'm suddenly in the mood for an Ally Carter Book Marathon of the Gallagher Girls &amp; Heist society Series and I'm even more impatient for Heist Society 3 to come out! Which is lucky it comes out next month! or I might have gone cray-cray! :D And the last Gallagher Girl book is hopefully coming out towards the end of the year, so THAT I'm definitely hyped about! since it was the Gallagher Girl Series that got me hooked into YA Books. <br /><br />In overall Double Crossed is a MUST-READ novella!!! :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="6298254286170080464" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_475841153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/475841153" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4845879-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335671607p2/4845879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/475841153?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/4845879-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer475841153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3963388223128264004">I wasn't sure how I was going to like the Gallagher Girls/ Heist society mix... But I loved it!!!!!!!<br/><br/>It was so fun to get inside Macey's, Abby's, and Hale's heads. To see how they think and what not. I really like how much action there was in such a short book. And I loved that you got to see how much Abby and Macey's Dad really do love her, and how she loves and respects both of them. I mean you kinda get to see it in the GG series but Ally Carter put more emphases into this story.<br/><br/>Kat and Hale </span>
  <span id="freeText3963388223128264004" style="display:none">I wasn't sure how I was going to like the Gallagher Girls/ Heist society mix... But I loved it!!!!!!!<br /><br />It was so fun to get inside Macey's, Abby's, and Hale's heads. To see how they think and what not. I really like how much action there was in such a short book. And I loved that you got to see how much Abby and Macey's Dad really do love her, and how she loves and respects both of them. I mean you kinda get to see it in the GG series but Ally Carter put more emphases into this story.<br /><br />Kat and Hale were so cute too. Not that you get to see a lot of them together. But it was cute to see what all they said about the other during their POV's. <br /><br />The ending was awesome. It totally leaves it open to them coming together in either Heist Society 3 or GG 6. I'm thinking more GG 6. But I can totally see it happening!<br /><br />I really liked reading this short story and am really hoping that Ally rights more of these! I can never get enough of her writing or these characters!!!!!!!! If you haven't read it yet, you should definitely give it a try!!!!<br /><br />Just a few of my favorite quotes to maybe wet your mouth enough to read it...<br /><br />Hale: "I'm sorry if I'm not fliring with you. I'm kind of spoken for."<br />Macey: "I'm sorry if I'm not disappointed. I kind of don't care."<br /><br />"Tell me what's going on."<br />"Pary crashers," Hale whispered. He watched Macey watching him. "Five, and they brought toys."<br />"Guns?" Kat guessed.<br />"Big ones," Hale said.<br />"you know this is what you get for doing a favor for your mother."<br /><br />"Cammie's going to be mad she missed this," Macey said to fill the silence.<br />"Excuse me?" Hale asked.<br />"Nothing." She shook her head. "I just...I have a friend who really likes air vents. And dumbwaiter shafts. And laundry chutes. Of course, the last time I was in a laundry chute, Cammie and I fell about a dozen stories..."<br />"well, that sounds like fun."<br />"it was either that or get kidnapped by terrorists, so I guess we got of easy."<br /><br />"Kat," Abby called, strolling in her direction. "Tell me about your boyfriend."<br />"Well...I don't know that he's my boyfriend. I mean...he's a boy. And he's my friend. And there's recently been the addition of kissing. But does that make us friends with benefits or-"<br />"Kat," Abby snapped.<br />"sorry,"<br /><br />"What are you doing next?"<br />Kat shrugged. "I might go to Rome. There's a Raphael there I kind of need to...aquire."<br />"That's funny." Macey laughed. "There's an ambassador's son there I kind of need to kidnap. Maybe we'll see each other around."<br /><br />Want more of this book? Go get it, it's free on amazon! Can't beat that!!!!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wv4OkWsDFatnPcWtmvS5YexaR+lTlFtgVCwen7tk17c//eLlw4a/h9z4AAhQJ4nj2xXKn5JLF+Uh7hqbD3ts4A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UHecSAH7q2lmqZ9xEXymbcxsKI0v5GGwvlCvgAvJ1uatdHA8qX4BRd1sWtTbr5bv+yOl++47LTXLkquEv9ZtsQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15078501795258751337">Ally Carter writes books about spies, thieves, and teenagers. She is the New York Times Best-selling author of the Gallagher Girls, Heist Society, and Embassy Row series. Her books have been published all over the world, in over twenty languages. <br/><br/>She encourages you to visit her online at allycarter.com and embassyrowbooks.com.</span>

        $('bookCover_13580928').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
